Conditions of Salam: Deferred Term and the Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute
Lists conditions and defends deferred term vs. Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five conditions for a valid salam contract, explain why the Hanafi school requires a deferred term, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Salam must be deferred with a known term; minimum one month per the relied-upon fatwa.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq outlines the five essential conditions for a valid salam (forward sale) contract. It then focuses on the crucial condition of a fixed term (ajal) and presents the Hanafi proof from hadith, along with a response to the Shafi'i view that salam can be immediate. Understanding this dispute clarifies the distinction between a valid deferred sale and an invalid immediate one.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that salam must be deferred; immediate salam is invalid. The minimum term is one month.
The text states 'وأقله شهر' (its minimum is a month).
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i allows salam to be immediate (hālan), relying on the general prohibition of selling what one does not possess.
The Shafi'i view is mentioned in the passage: 'وقال الشافعي يصح حالاً أيضاً'.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i argues that immediate delivery is permissible because the contract is like any sale, and the general prohibition of selling what one does not possess is not violated if the seller can deliver later.
The text says: 'لأنه عليها نهى عن بيع ما ليس عند الإنسان'.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi respond with the explicit hadith: 'من أسلم فليسلم في كيل معلوم ووزن معلوم إلى أجل معلوم' (Whoever pays salam, let him pay salam in a known measure, a known weight, and a known term). The word 'to a known term' indicates deferment is a condition. Also, the ability to deliver requires time, so a term is necessary.
The hadith is quoted in the text: 'إلى أجل معلوم'.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Hanafi law, immediate salam is batil (void); under Shafi'i it is valid. The minimum term for Hanafi is one month.
The practical consequence: a contract with delivery in two weeks is invalid in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والنوع والصفة والقدر والأجل، وأقله شهر، وقدر رأس المال في المكيل والموزون الأجل في الأصح وعليه الفتوى والمعدود، ومكان الإيفاء فيما له حمل أي في الذي والنوع أي والثاني بيان نوعه كالسهلية والحبلية في الحنطة والبزنى والمكتوم في التمر. (عيني) والصفة: أي والثالث: السلم. مطلقاً، ذلك عن بيان الصفة كالجيد والرديء والوسط (عيني) والقدر أي الرابع بيان القدر كعشرة أراد به أرطال. (ط) والأجل [ أي الخامس بيان الأجل المعلوم كشهر أو شهرين (ط)] أي وشرطه بيان الأجل المعلوم فلا يصح السلم إلا مؤجلا، وقال الشافعي يصح حالاً أيضاً؛ لأنه عليها نهى عن بيع ما ليس عند الإنسان، ورخص في ولنا قوله عليه: "من أسلم فليسلم في كيل معلوم ووزن معلوم إلى أجل معلوم"، فشرط فيه إعلام أجل كما شرط إعلام القدر؛ لأن المشروع بصفة لا يوجد بدون تلك الصفة، ولأن القدرة على تسليم المعقود عليه شرط فما به سبب القدرة وهو الأجل الذي يتمكن فيه من تحصيله رخصة لحاجة المقاييس، يكون شرطاً ضرورة، وأما تقدير الأجل فإلى المتعاقدين، وقيل: ثلاثة أيام؟ اعتباراً بشرط الخيار. وقيل: أكثر من نصف يوم، وقيل: إنه ينظر إلى مقدار المسلم فيه، وإلى عرف الناس في التأجيل في مثله، فإن أجل قدر ما يؤجل الناس في مثله ،جاز، وإلا فلا والفتوى على ما ذكره المصنف بقوله : "وأقله شهر"، روي . محمد؛ لأن ما دونه عاجل والشهر وما فوقه آجل [ رمز الحقائق: ٧٤/٢] (فتح)
The type, quality, quantity, and term, and its minimum is a month, and the amount of capital in weighed and measured [items] is the term according to the most correct opinion and upon it is the fatwa, and counted [items], and the place of delivery for what has carriage. That is: the second: statement of its type like al-Sahlia and al-Hablia in wheat and al-Bazni and al-Maktum in dates. (Ayni) And the quality: the third: statement of the quality like good, bad, and medium. (Ayni) And the quantity: the fourth: statement of the quantity like ten intended by it pounds. (T) And the term: the fifth: statement of the known term like a month or two months. (T) That is, its condition is the statement of the known term, so salam is not valid except deferred. And al-Shafi'i said it is valid immediately as well; because he relied on the prohibition of selling what one does not possess, and he permitted... And we have his statement (peace be upon him): 'Whoever pays salam, let him pay salam in a known measure, a known weight, and a known term.' So he made a condition of declaring the term just as he made a condition of declaring the quantity; because the legislated [contract] with a description does not exist without that description, and because the ability to deliver the subject matter is a condition, so that by which the ability occurs, which is the term enabling one to procure it, is a concession due to the need for analogies, it becomes a condition by necessity. As for the estimation of the term, it is up to the two contractors. And it was said: three days, considering the condition of option. And it was said: more than half a day. And it was said: it looks to the quantity of the subject matter of salam, and to the custom of people regarding deferment in its like. So if he sets a term that people defer in its like, it is permissible, otherwise not. And the fatwa is on what the author mentioned by his statement: 'And its minimum is a month', narrated by Muhammad; because what is less than that is immediate, and a month and above is deferred. (Fath).
Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and inter-madhhab dispute. It begins by listing the five conditions required for a valid salam (forward sale) contract: specifying the type (jins), kind (naw'), quality (sifah), quantity (qadr), and a fixed term (ajal). The Hanafi school holds that salam must be deferred and cannot be immediate. The minimum term is one month according to the relied-upon fatwa, as the author states. The commentary then explains each: for type, examples like types of wheat or dates; for quality, good, medium, bad; for quantity, a specific number like ten pounds; for term, one or two months. Then the passage presents the dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i, who allows salam to be immediate (hālan). The Hanafi proof is the hadith: 'Whoever pays salam, let him pay salam in a known measure, a known weight, and a known term.' The word 'to an appointed term' indicates deferment. The Hanafi reasoning is that the ability to deliver the subject matter requires time, so a term is necessary. The text then discusses various opinions on the minimum term (three days, half a day, custom) but confirms that the fatwa is on one month, as reported from Imam Muhammad. This is because anything less than a month is considered immediate ('ājil), while a month or more is deferred (ājil). Thus the lesson establishes the basic conditions and resolves the dispute in favor of the Hanafi position.

Key Terms
السلم (al-salam): A forward sale where the price is paid in advance for a defined commodity to be delivered at a future date.
الأجل (al-ajal): The fixed future term for delivery of the subject matter in salam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum term for a valid salam contract according to the Hanafi fatwa?
A) Three days
B) One month
C) Half a day
D) One year

Key Takeaway
A valid salam requires specification of type, kind, quality, quantity, and a deferred term of at least one month.

Place of Delivery in Salam for Carriage Goods: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Condition of specifying place of delivery for carriage goods in salam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Abu Hanifa's condition for specifying the place of delivery in salam for carriage goods, explain the opposing view of the Sahibayn, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
For goods requiring carriage, Abu Hanifa requires specifying the place of delivery; otherwise, uncertainty invalidates the contract.

This passage delves into an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether the place of delivery must be specified in a salam contract when the subject matter requires carriage. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your ability to handle conditions of validity in deferred sales, particularly how the Hanafi school balances potential dispute against contractual flexibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the point of dispute
Recognize that this lesson concerns salam (forward sale) and the condition of specifying the place of delivery (makān al-īfā') for goods that require carriage (ḥaml). The dispute is whether this specification is a condition for the contract's validity.
Ḥaml with fatḥa means the weight needing transport, with kasra means what is carried (like wheat).
2
State the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa)
Abu Hanifa holds that specifying the place of delivery is a condition (sharṭ) for validity. Without it, the contract is invalid because the value of goods may vary by location, leading to ignorance (jahālah) that causes dispute.
This is based on the principle of avoiding gharar (uncertainty).
3
State the opposing view of the Sahibayn
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that place specification is not a condition. Delivery defaults to the place of contract, but if the parties stipulate a place, it is valid. They analogize to other contracts where immediate delivery is not required.
The Sahibayn do not require specification, but if it is stipulated, it is honored.
4
Analyze the reasoning (ta'lil)
Both sides use qiyas and counter-analogies. The Sahibayn argue that since delivery is deferred, the place of contract suffices, similar to a loan. Abu Hanifa counters that deferral does not eliminate the need for location certainty, as differing values across places create dispute.
The text extends the dispute to price, hire, and division; for loan and damage, consensus rules.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The text declares Abu Hanifa's view as 'al-ṣaḥīḥ' (the correct one) and it is the relied-upon position for fatwa. The city is sufficient specification; a more precise place is not needed.
This tarjih is based on the need to prevent disputes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فيما له حمل [ أي السابع بيان مكان إيفاء المسلم فيه ومؤونة، والحمل بفتح الحاء: ثقل يحتاج في حمله إلى ظهر أو أجرة حمال، وبكسر الحاء ما يحمل كالبر ونحوه، هذا أيضاً عند أبي حنيفة، وقالا: ليس بشرط، ويوفيه في موضع العقد، ولكن إن شرطاه صح، وبه قالت الثلاثة؛ لأنه مكان الالتزام فيتعين لإيفاء ما التزمه كموضع من الأشياء، وما لا حمل له يوفيه حيث شاء، وقبض رأس المال المسلم إليه القرض والاستهلاك، وله أن التسليم غير واجب في الحال، فلا يتعين مكان العقد، وإذا لم يتعين بقي مجهولاً جهالة مفضية إلى المنازعة؛ لاختلاف القيم باختلاف الأماكن، وعلى هذا الخلاف الثمن والأجرة والقسمة، فعنده: يشترط بيان مكان الإيفاء وهو الصحيح، وعندهما: لا يشترط، وأما القرض والغصب والإتلاف فكالبيع بالاتفاق، فلا يشترط بيان مكان الإيفاء، وتعيين المصر يكفي. (عيني، فتح) الأشياء: كالبر والشعير والملح والماش. وما لا حمل :له وقيل ما لم يكن له حمل ومؤونة هو الذي يحمل مجاناً، وقيل: ما يمكن رفعه بيد واحدة والمؤونة الكلفة كالمسك والزعفران أي القليل منهما. يوفيه: أي يوفي المسلم إليه المسلم فيه حيث شاء؛ لعدم الاحتياج إلى بيان مكان الإيفاء، ولو عين مكاناً قيل: لا يتعين؛ لأنه لا يفيد، وقيل: يتعين؛ لأنه يفيد سقوط خطر الطريق. (فتح) حيث شاء لعدم الاحتياج إلى بيان مكان الإيفاء فيه بالإجماع.
As for what has carriage: the seventh condition: statement of the place of delivery of the subject matter of salam and its expense. Al-ḥaml with fatḥa on the ḥā: a weight needing a beast or wage of a porter to carry. With kasr on the ḥā: what is carried, like wheat and similar. This also according to Abu Hanifa, and the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: it is not a condition, and he delivers it at the place of contract, but if they stipulate it, it is valid. And the three (other imams) said that; because it is the place of obligation, so it is specified for delivery of what is obligated, like the place for things. And what has no carriage, he delivers it wherever he wishes. And the receipt of the capital from the one to whom salam is given, and loan and consumption, and he has that delivery is not obligatory immediately, so the place of contract is not specified. If it is not specified, it remains unknown, a ignorance leading to dispute due to difference in values by difference of places. And on this disagreement are the price, hire, and division. So according to him (Abu Hanifa), stating the place of delivery is a condition, and it is the correct view. According to them (the two), it is not a condition. As for loan, usurpation, and damage, they are like a sale by agreement, so stating the place of delivery is not a condition. And specifying the city is sufficient. (Ayni, Fath) The things: like wheat, barley, salt, and livestock. And what has no carriage: it was said, what has no carriage and expense is that which is carried for free, and it was said, what can be lifted with one hand, and the expense is the cost like musk and saffron, i.e., a little of them. He delivers it: i.e., the one to whom salam is given delivers the subject matter wherever he wishes; due to no need to state the place of delivery. And if he specifies a place, it was said: it is not specified because it is not beneficial; and it was said: it is specified because it removes the risk of the road. (Fath) Wherever he wishes, due to no need to state the place of delivery by consensus.
Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the condition of specifying the place of delivery for goods in a salam contract. Abu Hanifa holds that for items that require carriage (ḥaml), the place of delivery must be specified; otherwise, the contract is invalid due to uncertainty leading to disputes. His position is that the place is a necessary condition. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree, stating that it is not a condition; delivery may be at the place of the contract, but if the parties stipulate a place, it is valid. The passage also clarifies that for items without carriage (e.g., small valuable items like musk), no place need be specified, and delivery can be anywhere. The dispute extends to other contracts: for price, hire, and division similar disagreement exists. The passage notes that for loan, usurpation, and damage, by consensus no place specification is needed; specifying the city is sufficient. The text also discusses definitions of ḥaml (with fatḥa or kasra) and gives examples of items with and without carriage.

Key Terms
الحمل (al-ḥaml): Carriage; with fatḥa on ḥā: weight requiring transport, with kasra: what is carried (like wheat). Here used for items requiring transport expense.
مكان الإيفاء (makān al-īfā'): The place where the subject matter of salam is to be delivered.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The place of delivery must be specified
B) The place must be left unspecified
C) Delivery must be at the purchaser's home
D) No contract is valid for such items

Key Takeaway
For salam goods requiring carriage, the mufta bihi position is that specifying the place of delivery is a necessary condition to avoid invalidity due to uncertainty.

Receipt of Capital Before Separation in Salam
States the eighth condition of salam and its rationale.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the eighth condition for a valid salam contract and explain why receipt of capital before separation is required.

Core Idea
In salam, the capital must be received before the parties part to prevent a prohibited debt-for-debt exchange.

We now examine the eighth condition for a valid salam contract: that the capital must be received by the seller before the parties separate. This condition ensures the contract does not become an exchange of debt for debt, which is prohibited. The passage also discusses how this condition applies to different types of capital and mentions a difference with Imam Malik.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position
State that the capital must be received in the contract session before the parties separate. This is a condition for the contract's continuance (shart baqa'), not formation.
2
Understand the rationale
The rationale is based on analogy (qiyas) to sarf (currency exchange) and the prohibition of debt-for-debt exchange. Receipt ensures an immediate price for a deferred commodity.
3
Note the implications for khiyar
Stipulating an option (khiyar) in the capital is not allowed because it prevents complete receipt. Similarly, khiyar al-ru'ya does not apply to the subject matter (since it is a debt), but khiyar al-'ayb applies to the capital if it is a specific good.
4
Compare with the Maliki view
Imam Malik allows a delay of a day or two if customarily considered immediate. This is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on different weight given to custom.
5
Distinguish between conditions of formation and continuance
The text explicitly states this condition is for the continuance of the contract, not its formation. If the parties separate without receipt, the contract becomes invalid (fasid) after initially being valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقبض رأس المال : [ أي الشرط الثامن: وهو شرط بقائه قبض إلخ. (عيني)] عطف على "بيان الجنس"، أي شرط جوازه قبض رأس المال قبل افتراق المتعاقدين؛ لأن السلم يبتني على أخذ عاجل بآجل، وذلك بالقبض قبل الافتراق كما في الصرف، ولا فرق في ذلك بين أن يكون رأس المال مما يتعين أو لا ؛ لأنه فيما لا يتعين يلزم الافتراق عن دين بدين، وهو منهي عنه، وأما إذا كان عيناً، فاشتراط القبض جواز الاستحسان إعمالاً للمقتضى الشرعي ولابد من تسليمه إليه ليتصرف فيه، فيقدر على تسليم المسلم فيه، ولهذا لا يجوز اشتراط الخيار فيه؛ لأنه يمنع تمام القبض. وكذا لا يثبت في المسلم فيه خيار الرؤية؛ لأنه غير مفيد؛ إذ هو دين في الذمة بخلاف خيار العيب في رأس المال، وخيار الرؤية فيه حيث يثبتان فيه إذا كان مما يتعين بالتعيين كالعروض، وعند مالك لو ترك قبض رأس المال يوماً أو يومين جاز؛ لأنه يعد عاجلاً عرفاً، وهذا الشرط شرط بقاء العقد لا شرط انعقاده، إلى هنا تم عدد الشروط الثمانية والشرط التاسع الذي لم يذكر الشيخ هو القدرة على تحصيل المسلم فيه بأن يوجد من حين العقد إلى حين المحل، وإنما لم يذكره استغناء بما تقدم من عدم جواز السلم في المنقطع.
And receipt of the capital: the eighth condition: it is a condition of the contract's continuance, receipt etc. (Ayni) Appended to 'statement of the type', i.e., a condition of its validity is receipt of the capital before the separation of the two contractors; because salam is based on taking an immediate [price] for a deferred [commodity], and that is by receipt before separation as in ṣarf. And there is no difference in that whether the capital is determinate or not; because in what is not determinate, separation on a debt for a debt would occur, and that is prohibited. As for if it is a specific good, then stipulating receipt is permitted by istiḥsān, acting upon the legal requirement, and it is necessary to hand it over to him so he can deal with it, enabling him to deliver the subject matter. For this reason, stipulating an option (khiyār) in it is not permitted, because it prevents complete receipt. Similarly, the option of sight (khiyār al-ru'ya) is not established in the subject matter of salam, because it is not beneficial since it is a debt in the liability, unlike the option of defect (khiyār al-'ayb) in the capital, and the option of sight in it, where they are established if it is determinate by specification like goods. According to Malik, if he leaves the receipt of the capital for a day or two, it is permissible, because it is considered immediate by custom. This condition is a condition of the contract's continuance, not a condition of its formation. Up to here ends the number of eight conditions. And the ninth condition that the author did not mention is the ability to procure the subject matter, i.e., that it exists from the time of contract to the time of delivery. He omitted it because he relied on what preceded about the impermissibility of salam in what is unavailable.
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage covers the eighth condition for a valid salam contract: the capital (ra's al-māl) must be received by the seller before the contracting parties separate from the session. The reasoning is that salam is an exchange of an immediate payment for a deferred commodity; thus, the immediate payment must be complete to avoid a prohibited exchange of debt for debt. This condition applies whether the capital is determinate (like a specific coin) or not. The text then discusses that stipulating a khiyār (option) in the capital is not allowed because it would prevent full receipt. Similarly, the khiyār al-ru'ya (option of sight) does not apply to the subject matter (since it is a debt), but options of defect and sight do apply to the capital if it is a specific good. A difference with Imam Malik is noted: he allows a delay of a day or two for receipt, considering it immediate by custom. The passage concludes by noting that these eight conditions are for the validity of the contract, and a ninth condition (ability to procure the subject matter) is omitted because it was already covered.

Key Terms
رأس المال (ra's al-māl): The capital or price paid in advance by the purchaser in a salam contract.
خيار العيب (khiyār al-'ayb): Option of defect; the right to annul the contract due to a hidden defect in the object.
خيار الرؤية (khiyār al-ru'ya): Option of sight; the right to rescind a contract after seeing an unseen object.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens if the parties separate before the capital is received in a salam contract?
A) The contract becomes void.
B) The contract remains valid if both parties agree.
C) The contract is suspended until payment.
D) The contract is valid but the seller must chase the buyer.

Key Takeaway
The capital in salam must be received in the contract session before the parties part to avoid a prohibited debt-for-debt exchange.

The 17 Conditions of Salam from al-Ghayah
Summarizes 17 conditions for valid salam from al-Ghayah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the 17 conditions for a valid salam contract and distinguish between those related to the capital and those related to the subject matter.

Core Idea
A valid salam contract requires 17 precise conditions: 6 on the capital and 11 on the subject matter, ensuring no uncertainty or ribā.

Salam is a forward sale where the price is paid in advance for future delivery of a commodity. To prevent gharar (uncertainty) and ribā, Hanafi scholars outlined exactly 17 conditions. This lesson presents them as a memorization anchor from the work al-Ghayah, a concise text often committed to memory.

Guided Path
1
Understand the division
Note that the 17 conditions are split into two groups: 6 conditions related to the capital (ra's al-māl) and 11 related to the subject matter (muslim fīh). This division helps approach memorization systematically.
2
Memorize the 6 capital conditions
These are: (1) statement of type, (2) statement of kind, (3) statement of quality, (4) declaring quantity, (5) coins being minted (Abu Hanifa; not required by the two companions), and (6) the capital must be advanced and received before the parties separate.
Condition 5 is subject to intra-Hanafi dispute.
3
Memorize the 11 subject matter conditions
These include: (1-4) same as capital: type, kind, quality, quantity; (5) no ribā al-faḍl attributes in the countervalues; (6) subject matter must be determinable by specification; (7) must be deferred; (8) must be available; (9) contract must be final (no option of condition); (10) place of delivery stated for items needing carriage; (11) subject matter well-defined by description, using the four categories: makīl, mawzūn, madhrū', 'adadī mutaqārib.
These ensure certainty.
4
Apply the conditions to examples
Practice identifying which condition might be violated in hypothetical salam scenarios. For example, if the delivery place is not specified for heavy goods, condition 10 is missing.
Practical application solidifies memory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي "الغاية": شرائط صحة السلم سبعة عشر : ستة في رأس المال، وأحد عشر في المسلم فيه، أما الذي في رأس المال، فبيان الجنس وبيان النوع وبيان الصفة وإعلام قدر رأس المال وكون الدراهم والدنانير منقودة عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما ليس بشرط، وتعجيل رأس المال، وقبضه قبل الافتراق بأبدانهما، وأما التي في المسلم فيه، فبيان الجنس وبيان النوع وبيان الصفة وإعلام قدر المسلم فيه وأن لا يشتمل البدلان على أحد وصفي علة ربا الفضل، وهو القدر أو الجنس، وأن يكون المسلم فيه مما يتعين بالتعيين، وأن يكون مؤجلاً، وأن لا ينقطع، وأن يكون العقد باتاً ليس فيه خيار الشرط، وبيان مكان الإيفاء فيما له حمل ومؤونة، وكون المسلم فيه مضبوطاً بالوصف كالأجناس الأربعة أي المكيل والموزون والمذروع والعددي المتقارب. (عيني، فتح)
And in al-Ghayah: The conditions of validity of salam are seventeen: six concerning the capital, and eleven concerning the subject matter of salam. As for those concerning the capital: statement of the type, statement of the kind, statement of the quality, declaring the quantity of the capital, that the dirhams and dinars are minted (according to Abu Hanifa; according to them it is not a condition), and advancement of the capital and its receipt before separation with their bodies. As for those concerning the subject matter: statement of the type, statement of the kind, statement of the quality, declaring the quantity of the subject matter, that the two countervalues do not include one of the two attributes of the cause of ribā al-faḍl, which is quantity or type, that the subject matter is such that it can be determined by specification, that it is deferred, that it is not unavailable, that the contract is final without an option of condition, statement of the place of delivery for what has carriage and expense, and that the subject matter is well-defined by description like the four categories: measured by volume, weighed, measured by length, and counted items that are similar. (Ayni, Fath)
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage is a summary listing of the 17 conditions for a valid salam contract as stated in the work al-Ghayah. It divides them into six conditions related to the capital (ra's al-māl) and eleven related to the subject matter (muslim fīh). For the capital: it must specify type, kind, quality, quantity; according to Abu Hanifa the coins must be minted (but the two companions disagree); and the capital must be paid and received before separation. For the subject matter: it must specify type, kind, quality, quantity; it must not involve ribā al-faḍl in terms of quantity or type; it must be determinable by specification; it must be deferred; it must be available (not unavailable); the contract must be final without khiyār al-sharṭ; the place of delivery must be stated for items requiring carriage; and it must be well-defined by description, similar to the four categories: makīl (measured by volume), mawzūn (weighed), madhrū' (measured by length), and 'adadī mutaqārib (counted items that are similar). This is a concise memorization anchor for students.

Key Terms
ربا الفضل (ribā al-faḍl): The prohibited excess in exchange of similar items; its causes (illa) are quantity and type.
المسلم فيه (al-muslim fīh): The subject matter of the salam contract; the commodity to be delivered at the future date.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) 20

Key Takeaway
A valid salam contract requires 17 precise conditions, divided into 6 for capital and 11 for subject matter, all aimed at removing uncertainty and ribā.

Specifying Place of Delivery in Salam: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on specifying place of delivery in salam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi mufta bihi on specifying place of delivery in salam, distinguish between goods with and without transport cost, and explain why Abu Hanifa's view is preferred.

Core Idea
For goods with transport cost, Abu Hanifa requires place specification; without it, the contract risks invalidity.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether specifying the exact place of delivery is a condition for a valid salam contract. While for goods without transport cost the seller may deliver anywhere by consensus, for goods with cost Abu Hanifa requires specification to avoid uncertainty, whereas the Sahibayn do not. We will analyze their proofs and the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish goods by transport cost
Identify whether the subject matter of salam has transport cost (ma'ūna) or not. Goods like wheat, barley, salt have cost; items like musk or saffron in small quantity do not.
This distinction is the key trigger for the dispute.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and proof
For goods with cost, Abu Hanifa requires specifying the place of delivery. His proof: without specification, uncertainty arises because values differ by location, leading to dispute (munāza'a).
This is the mufta bihi view.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and proof
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad do not require specification. They analogize salam to loan, usurpation, and destruction where place is not specified by consensus, and note that delivery is not immediate.
They focus on the non-obligatory nature of delivery at contract.
4
Identify the practical consequence and tarjih
If place is not specified, Abu Hanifa deems the contract fasid until specification; Sahibayn uphold validity. The text declares Abu Hanifa's view 'as-sahīh' (correct), making it the operative ruling.
The thamarah al-khilaf is whether the contract is valid without specification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب السلم من الأشياء، وما لا حمل له يوفيه حيث شاء، وقبض رأس المال المسلم إليه القرض والاستهلاك، وله أن التسليم غير واجب في الحال، فلا يتعين مكان العقد، وإذا لم يتعين بقي مجهولاً جهالة مفضية إلى المنازعة؛ لاختلاف القيم باختلاف الأماكن، وعلى هذا الخلاف الثمن والأجرة والقسمة، فعنده: يشترط بيان مكان الإيفاء وهو الصحيح، وعندهما: لا يشترط، وأما القرض والغصب والإتلاف فكالبيع بالاتفاق، فلا يشترط بيان مكان الإيفاء، وتعيين المصر يكفي. (عيني، فتح) الأشياء: كالبر والشعير والملح والماش. وما لا حمل :له وقيل ما لم يكن له حمل ومؤونة هو الذي يحمل مجاناً، وقيل: ما يمكن رفعه بيد واحدة والمؤونة الكلفة كالمسك والزعفران أي القليل منهما. يوفيه: أي يوفي المسلم إليه المسلم فيه حيث شاء؛ لعدم الاحتياج إلى بيان مكان الإيفاء، ولو عين مكاناً قيل: لا يتعين؛ لأنه لا يفيد، وقيل: يتعين؛ لأنه يفيد سقوط خطر الطريق. (فتح) حيث شاء لعدم الاحتياج إلى بيان مكان الإيفاء فيه بالإجماع.
Chapter of Salam. From things that have no transport cost, he delivers it wherever he wishes. The receipt of capital is like loan and consumption. And delivery is not obligatory immediately, so the place of contract is not specified. When it is not specified, it remains unknown, a ignorance leading to dispute because values differ by place. And upon this analogy are the price, wage, and division. According to him (Abu Hanifa), specification of place of delivery is required, and it is correct. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is not required. As for loan, usurpation, and destruction, it is like sale by consensus: place of delivery is not required, and specifying the city suffices. (Ayni, Fath) 'Things': like wheat, barley, salt, and cattle. 'What has no transport cost': it is said what has no transport and expense, that is carried for free; also said what can be lifted by one hand. 'Expense' is cost like musk and saffron, i.e., a little of them. 'He delivers it': i.e., the seller delivers the salam goods wherever he wishes, because no need to specify place of delivery. If he specified a place, some said it is not binding because it is useless; some said it is binding because it removes the risk of the road. (Fath) 'Wherever he wishes' because there is no need to specify place of delivery by consensus.
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the condition of specifying the place of delivery (makān al-īfā') in a salam contract. The commentary opens by distinguishing between goods with and without transport cost (haml wa ma'ūna). For goods without such cost—like musk, saffron, or items easily carried—the seller may deliver anywhere, as there is no need for specification. For goods with transport cost, Abu Hanifa (ra) requires specifying the place of delivery to avoid uncertainty that leads to dispute, since values differ by location. His position is deemed correct (as-sahīh) and is the relied-upon view. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) do not require specification, analogizing to loan, usurpation, and destruction where place is not specified by consensus. The passage also notes that specifying the city suffices for goods with transport cost. The dispute extends to price, wage, and division in similar contracts.

Key Terms
مكان الإيفاء (makān al-īfā'): The specific place where delivery of the salam goods is to be made.
ما لا حمل له (mā lā hamla lahu): Goods that have no transport cost, i.e., can be carried easily for free.
المؤونة (al-ma'ūna): Expense or cost of transport; the burden of moving goods.

Condition of Receiving Capital Before Separation in Salam
Ruling on necessity of capital receipt before parties separate

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition of capital receipt in salam, explain its qiyas to sarf, and distinguish between the treatment of khiyar in capital vs. salam goods.

Core Idea
Capital must be received before separation to avoid prohibited debt-for-debt exchange.

Salam is a unique sale where payment is immediate but delivery is deferred. For this contract to be valid, the Hanafi school insists that the capital (price) must be physically or constructively received before the parties leave the session. This lesson unpacks the eighth condition of salam, its proof by analogy to currency exchange (sarf), and the implications for stipulating options.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition and its placement
Locate 'شرط قبض رأس المال' as the eighth condition of salam. Note that it requires receipt of capital before the parties separate (قبل افتراق المتعاقدين).
This is a condition for the contract's continuation, not its initial conclusion.
2
Understand the legal reason (illah)
The text explains that salam is built on 'prompt taking for deferred delivery'. If parties separate without receipt, it becomes a sale of debt for debt (dayn bi dayn), which is prohibited. This is the core rationale.
The prohibition of dayn bi dayn is a major principle in Islamic finance.
3
Apply the analogy to sarf
The requirement is analogous to currency exchange (sarf) where immediate hand-to-hand transfer is mandatory. Just as in sarf, salam requires qabd before separation to prevent riba or uncertainty.
Qiyas jali: clear analogy based on shared illah of immediate exchange.
4
Note the scope: both 'ayn and dayn
The condition applies whether the capital is a specific object ('ayn) or a debt (dayn). In the case of a specific object, istihsan upholds the condition to fulfill the legal objective. No difference is made.
This refutes the misconception that receipt is only needed for non-specific capital.
5
Derive rulings on options (khiyar)
Because complete qabd is essential, stipulating khiyar al-shart in the capital is invalid as it prevents full possession. Similarly, khiyar ar-ru'ya does not apply to the salam goods (being a debt), but options like khiyar al-'ayb apply to the capital if it is a determinate commodity.
This shows the practical effect of the condition on contract terms.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقبض رأس المال : [ أي الشرط الثامن: وهو شرط بقائه قبض إلخ. (عيني)] عطف على "بيان الجنس"، أي شرط جوازه قبض رأس المال قبل افتراق المتعاقدين؛ لأن السلم يبتني على أخذ عاجل بآجل، وذلك بالقبض قبل الافتراق كما في الصرف، ولا فرق في ذلك بين أن يكون رأس المال مما يتعين أو لا ؛ لأنه فيما لا يتعين يلزم الافتراق عن دين بدين، وهو منهي عنه، وأما إذا كان عيناً، فاشتراط القبض جواز الاستحسان إعمالاً للمقتضى الشرعي ولابد من تسليمه إليه ليتصرف فيه، فيقدر على تسليم المسلم فيه، ولهذا لا يجوز اشتراط الخيار فيه؛ لأنه يمنع تمام القبض. وكذا لا يثبت في المسلم فيه خيار الرؤية؛ لأنه غير مفيد؛ إذ هو دين في الذمة بخلاف خيار العيب في رأس المال، وخيار الرؤية فيه حيث يثبتان فيه إذا كان مما يتعين بالتعيين كالعروض، وعند مالك لو ترك قبض رأس المال يوماً أو يومين جاز؛ لأنه يعد عاجلاً عرفاً، وهذا الشرط شرط بقاء العقد لا شرط انعقاده، إلى هنا تم عدد الشروط الثمانية والشرط التاسع الذي لم يذكر الشيخ هو القدرة على تحصيل المسلم فيه بأن يوجد من حين العقد إلى حين المحل، وإنما لم يذكره استغناء بما تقدم من عدم جواز السلم في المنقطع.
And receipt of capital: i.e., the eighth condition: it is a condition of its continuance, receipt etc. (Ayni). It is connected to 'specification of type', i.e., a condition of its validity is receipt of capital before the parties separate, because salam is built on a prompt taking for a deferred one, and that is by receipt before separation as in sarf (currency exchange). There is no difference in that between whether the capital is determinate or not, because in the case of what is not determinate, separation on debt for debt occurs, which is prohibited. As for when it is a specific object, then stipulating receipt is permissible by istihsan, acting on the legal requirement, and it must be handed over to him so he can dispose of it, enabling him to deliver the salam goods. For this reason, stipulating a condition of option (khiyar) in it is not allowed, because it prevents complete receipt. Likewise, option of sight (khiyar ar-ru'ya) is not established in the salam goods, because it is useless, as it is a debt in the dhimmah, unlike option of defect (khiyar al-'ayb) in the capital, and option of sight in it when it is determinate by specification like commodities. According to Malik, if one delays receipt of capital for a day or two, it is permissible, because it is considered prompt by custom. This condition is a condition for the continuance of the contract, not a condition for its validity. Up to here, the eight conditions are completed. The ninth condition, which the author did not mention, is the ability to obtain the salam goods, i.e., that it exists from the time of contract to the time of delivery. He did not mention it, relying on what preceded about the impermissibility of salam in non-existent goods.
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the condition of receiving the capital (ra's al-māl) before the contracting parties separate in a salam contract. The eight condition is that the capital must be paid and received in the session. The reason is that salam is an exchange of immediate payment for deferred delivery; thus, if the parties separate without receipt, it becomes a forbidden sale of debt for debt (dayn bi dayn). This applies whether the capital is a specific object ('ayn) or a debt (dayn). If it is a specific object, the receipt condition is established by istihsan (juristic preference) to fulfill the legal requirement. Consequently, stipulating a condition of option (khiyar al-shart) in the capital is invalid because it prevents complete possession. Similarly, the salam goods being a debt, option of sight does not apply, unlike options for defect or sight on the capital if it is a determinate commodity. The passage also notes that Imam Malik allows a delay of a day or two customarily. This condition is for the continuation of the contract, not its initial validity, meaning if the parties separate without receipt, the contract becomes fasid (invalid) but not batil from the start. The text then lists the ninth condition (ability to deliver) which is implicit.

Key Terms
قبض (qabd): Physical or constructive receipt and possession of the capital in the contract session.
دين بدين (dayn bi dayn): Exchange of a debt for a debt, prohibited in salam if parties separate without receipt.
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): Option to rescind the contract within a stipulated period.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because option is only allowed in the salam goods
D) Because the capital must be a debt

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the validity of a salam contract depends on the buyer taking possession of the capital before the parties separate, to avoid the prohibited sale of debt for debt.

Salam with Mixed Capital: Debt and Cash
Ruling on salam where part of capital is a debt owed by the counterparty

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on salam with mixed capital (debt and cash), distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn, and Zufar, and explain why the invalidity does not spread.

Core Idea
In salam, if part of the capital is a debt, only that part is invalid; the defect does not spread to the cash portion.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses a nuanced scenario in salam (advance payment sale): what happens when the capital includes a debt owed by the seller? The Hanafi masters differ on whether such a defect nullifies the entire contract or only the problematic portion. Understanding this ruling requires careful attention to the timing of the defect and the nature of the capital.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and the ruling
Read the passage to understand the scenario: a person gives salam for a karr of wheat with 200 dirhams, of which 100 is a debt owed by the seller and 100 is cash. Note that the ruling declares the debt portion invalid but the cash portion valid.
The invalidity is described as 'batil' in the text, but commentators clarify it is fasid (voidable) due to a later defect.
2
Locate the different Hanafi positions
Identify Zufar's position that the entire contract is invalid (batil). Then note that Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that only the debt portion is invalid.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Analyze the dalil aqli for the majority view
The passage provides a rational proof (dalil aqli): the contract was valid at inception because the debt was not specified as capital; the defect arises only later due to separation (tafarruq) without receiving the debt. Since the defect is incidental (tari'), it does not spread to the valid cash portion.
Contrast with Zufar's reasoning: he considers the acceptance conditional on the debt, making the contract invalid from the start.
4
Consider the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
According to the majority, if the buyer pays both portions before separation, the entire contract becomes valid. Zufar would still hold it invalid. Also, if the capital is of two types (e.g., dirhams and dinars), the ruling differs based on whether the capital amount for each type is specified.
This shows how the ikhtilaf affects actual transactions.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The passage indicates that the majority view (Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn) is the relied-upon position. Zufar's view is a valid minority opinion within the school but is not acted upon.
Knowledge of intra-madhhab tarjih is essential for ifta'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قبل الافتراق، فإن أسلم مائتي درهم في كرّ بر مائةً ديناً عليه، ومائة نقداً، فالسلمُ صفة المائة أي على مسلم إليه أي منقودة في الدين باطل، ولا يصحُ التصرّف في رأس المال والمسلم فيه قبل القبض بشركة أي على مسلم إليه أو تولية. أو مرابحة ولو ممن عليه قبل الافتراق بالأبدان أي افتراق كل واحد من المتعاقدين عندنا. (عيني، معدن) کر بر: بضم الكاف وتشديد الراء: ستون قفيزا، والقفيز اثنا عشر صاعا (ط) عيني باطل: لافتراقهما عن دين بدين، وليس المعنى أنه انعقد باطلاً في حصة الدين بل هو صحيح، والمفسد طارئ عليه بافتراقهما، فلم يسر الفساد إلى حصة المائة الثانية، ولهذا لو نقد مأتين قبل الافتراق، صح في الكل، وعند زفر: السلم باطل في الكل؛ لأنه جعل القبول في الدين شرطاً لصحته في الآخر، فيفسد في الكل ولنا أن العقد وقع صحيحاً؛ لعدم تعين الدين. ثم فساده في البعض طارئ، فلا يتعدى، وهذا إذا كان رأس المال والمسلم فيه من نوع واحد، أما إذا كان رأس المال من نوعين بأن أسلم إلى رجل في كر بر عشرة من الدراهم المعينة، وعشرة من الدنانير التي عليه، فلا يجوز في حق الدنانير إجماعاً، وفي الدراهم كذلك عنده؛ لجهالة ما يخصها من المسلم فيه، خلافاً لهما، بناء على أن إعلام رأس المال ليس بشرط عندهما، وأما إذا كان المسلم فيه من نوعين بأن أسلم مائة درهم في كر بر وكر شعير، و لم يبين رأس مال كل واحد لا يجوز عنده. (عيني، فتح)
Before separation, if one gives salam of two hundred dirhams for a karr of wheat, with one hundred being a debt owed to him, and one hundred cash, then the salam of the one hundred (the debt) is invalid, but the salam of the cash portion is valid. Disposal of the capital and the salam goods before receipt is invalid, whether by partnership, assignment, or profit-sharing, even if from the debtor before separation of bodies, i.e., the separation of each of the two parties in our view. (Ayni, Ma'dan) Karr burr: with damma on kaf and tashdid on ra: sixty qafiz, and a qafiz is twelve sa'. (T) Ayni: 'batil' because they separate on debt for debt. The meaning is not that it was invalid from the start in the debt portion, but rather it was valid, and the invalidating factor later arose due to separation, so it does not spread to the second hundred portion. Therefore, if he paid both two hundred before separation, the whole is valid. According to Zufar: the whole salam is invalid because he made acceptance contingent on the debt, so it all becomes invalid. Our argument: the contract occurred validly because the debt was not specified. Then its invalidity in part is incidental, so it does not extend. This is when the capital and the salam goods are of one type. But if the capital is of two types - e.g., one gives salam for a karr of wheat with ten specific dirhams and ten dinars owed to him - then it is impermissible for the dinars by consensus, and also for the dirhams according to him (Abu Hanifa) due to ignorance of the share of the salam goods from each, contrary to the two (Sahibayn) because specification of capital is not a condition according to them. And if the salam goods are of two types - e.g., one gives salam for a karr of wheat and a karr of barley with one hundred dirhams, and he does not specify the capital for each - it is impermissible according to him. (Ayni, Fath)
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific case in salam: when the capital (ra's al-māl) partially consists of a debt owed by the seller to the buyer. The ruling distinguishes between the portion of capital that is debt and that which is cash. The debt portion is invalid because the parties would separate on a debt-for-debt exchange, which is prohibited. However, the invalidity does not affect the cash portion; it remains valid. If the entire capital is paid before separation, the whole contract becomes valid. Zufar (a Hanafi scholar) disagrees, arguing that the entire contract is invalid because the acceptance was made contingent on the debt. The Hanafi response is that the contract was valid at inception (since the debt was not specified as capital) and the defect only arises later due to separation, so it does not spread. The passage also discusses variations: if the capital consists of two different types (dirhams and dinars), then the consensus is that the dinar portion is invalid, and Abu Hanifa extends this to both types due to uncertainty about what portion of the salam goods corresponds to each. The Sahibayn differ because they do not require specifying the capital amount for each type. When the salam goods are of two types without allocation of capital, the salam is invalid.

Key Terms
مائة ديناً عليه (mi'at dainan 'alayh): One hundred (dirhams) that the seller owes to the buyer as a debt.
طارئ (tāri'): Incidental; a defect that arises after the contract is validly concluded.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi view, what happens to a salam contract if part of the capital is a debt owed by the seller to the buyer?
A) The entire contract is invalid (batil)
B) The debt portion is invalid, but the cash portion remains valid
C) The contract is valid only if the entire capital is paid before separation
D) The contract is valid only if the debt is forgiven

Key Takeaway
When salam capital includes a debt, only the debt portion is invalid; the invalidity does not spread to the cash portion.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Prohibition of Disposal of Salam Goods Before Receipt
Ruling forbidding sale or transfer of salam goods before possession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on disposing of salam goods or capital before receipt and identify which transactions are prohibited.

Core Idea
Any disposal of salam goods or capital before receipt is invalid because it is like selling what you do not possess.

In a salam contract, the buyer pays in advance for goods to be delivered later. Until the seller delivers the goods, the buyer does not legally possess them. This lesson explains why any transaction involving those goods—or even the capital—before physical receipt is prohibited and invalid, covering common forms like sale, partnership, and assignment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what the passage forbids: any tasarruf (legal disposition) of the salam goods or the capital before qabd (receipt). The ruling is that such acts are invalid (la yasihh) and prohibited.
2
Understand the reasoning
The salam goods are treated like a sold item (mabī'). The general rule prohibits selling or disposing of a movable item before taking possession. Similarly, the capital must be received in the session, so any transaction that prevents that is invalid.
Analogy (qiyas) to the Hadith: 'Do not sell what you do not possess.'
3
Distinguish the forms of prohibited disposal
The passage lists specific examples: sale, substitution (ibdal), partnership (sharika), assignment at cost (tawliya), and profit-sharing (murabaha). All are prohibited because they constitute a transfer of ownership before possession.
4
Apply to the given scenarios
Work through the examples: a salam buyer who takes a partner in the undelivered wheat, or sells it back to the seller at cost or with profit, each is invalid. The same applies to gifting the capital before the seller receives it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يصح التصرف إلخ ومن صور التصرف في رأس المال : أن يأخذ بدل رأس المال شيئاً آخر، ومنها أيضاً: أن يهب رأس المال من رب السلم قبل القبض. ومن صور التصرف في المسلم فيه قبل القبض: أن يشرك غيره فيه أو يبيعه أو يهبه قبل القبض، وجه عدم جواز التصرف أن المسلم فيه مبيع، والتصرف في المبيع المنقول قبل القبض لا يجوز، ورأس المال مستحق القبض في المجلس، والتصرف فيه مفوت له فلا يجوز والتصرف المنفي يشمل البيع، حتى لو باع رب السلم المسلم فيه من المسلم إليه بأكثر من رأس المال لا يصح، ويشمل الاستبدال حتى إذا استبدل المسلم فيه بجنس آخر لا يجوز؛ لكونه بيع المنقول قبل قبضه، وكذا الاستبدال برأس مال السلم لا يجوز؛ لكونه يفوت القبض المشروط؛ لأن لرأس المال شبهاً بالمبيع، فلا يجوز التصرف فيه قبل القبض. (عيني، فتح) قبل القبض: أي قبل قبض المسلم إليه رأس المال، وقبل قبض رب السلم المسلم فيه. (عيني) بشركة: صورتها: رجل أسلم عشرة دارهم في كر حنطة، فجاء آخر إليه وقال له خذ مني خمسة دراهم وأشركني في الحنطة التي أسلمت فيها" فأشركه فيها لا يجوز. (مسكين) أو تولية صورتها أسلم رجل عشرة دراهم في كر حنطة، فجاء رجل آخر إلى هذا الذي أسلم وقال له: "بع" مني الحنطة التي أسلمت فيها بما أسلمت" فباعها بعشرة تولية لا يجوز، وكذا إذا باعها مرابحة على العشرة لا يجوز أيضاً؛ لأن المسلم فيه مبيع، والتصرف فيه قبل القبض لا يجوز، وفي التولية تمليك كله بعوض، وفي الشركة تمليك بعضه بعوض، فلا يجوز رمز الحقائق: ٧٦/٢] (فتح)
And disposal is not valid, etc. Among the forms of disposal of the capital are: taking something else in exchange for the capital, and also gifting the capital to the salam buyer before receipt. Among the forms of disposal of the salam goods before receipt are: making someone a partner in it, or selling it, or gifting it before receipt. The reason for impermissibility is that the salam goods are a sold item, and disposal of a movable sold item before receipt is not allowed. The capital is required to be received in the session, and disposal of it prevents that, so it is not allowed. The prohibited disposal includes sale, so even if the salam buyer sells the salam goods to the seller for more than the capital, it is invalid. It includes substitution, so if he substitutes the salam goods for another type, it is invalid because it is selling a movable before receipt. Likewise, substitution for the capital of salam is invalid because it defeats the required receipt, as the capital resembles a sold item, so disposal before receipt is not allowed. (Ayni, Fath) 'Before receipt' means before the seller receives the capital and before the buyer receives the salam goods. (Ayni) 'By partnership': its form: a man gives salam of ten dirhams for a karr of wheat. Another person comes to him and says, 'Take five dirhams from me and make me a partner in the wheat for which you gave salam.' So he makes him a partner, it is not allowed. (Miskin) 'Or assignment' (tawliya): its form: a man gives salam of ten dirhams for a karr of wheat. Another man comes to him and says, 'Sell me the wheat for which you gave salam for the same amount.' So he sells it for ten dirhams by tawliya, it is not allowed. Likewise, if he sells it by murabaha (cost-plus) for ten dirhams, it is also not allowed, because the salam goods are a sold item, and disposal before receipt is not allowed. In tawliya, it is transfer of full ownership for compensation; in partnership, it is transfer of partial ownership for compensation, so it is not allowed. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/76) (Fath)
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that any disposal (tasarruf) of the capital or the salam goods before receipt (qabd) is invalid. The reasoning is that the salam goods are a sold item (mabī'), and selling a movable before taking possession is prohibited by Hadith ('Do not sell what you do not possess'). Similarly, the capital is required to be received in the session, so any transaction that prevents receipt—like exchanging it for something else—is invalid. The prohibition covers sale, substitution, partnership (sharika), assignment (tawliya), and profit-sharing (murabaha). Even selling back to the original seller (buyer's equivalent) is not allowed. Examples illustrate: if the buyer of salam (muslam) makes someone else a partner in the goods before receipt, it is invalid; likewise selling by tawliya (transfer at cost) or murabaha. The capital is treated like a sold item in this context, so similar restrictions apply before receipt.

Key Terms
التصرف (al-tasarruf): Any legal disposition such as sale, gift, partnership, or substitution involving the salam goods or capital before receipt.
تولية (tawliya): Transfer of ownership of goods to another at the same cost paid, without profit.
مرابحة (murabaha): Sale at cost plus a stated profit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In salam, why is it invalid for the buyer to make someone a partner in the salam goods before receiving them?
A) Because partnership is not allowed in debt
B) Because it constitutes a disposal of the sold item before possession
C) Because the seller's consent is required
D) Because the goods are still with the seller

Key Takeaway
Any act of disposal (sale, gift, partnership, substitution) of salam goods or capital before physical receipt is invalid, as it violates the principle that one cannot sell or transfer what one does not possess.

Salam with Mixed Capital: Cash and Debt
States the ruling when salam capital is partly cash and partly a debt owed by the seller.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when salam capital is partly cash and partly a debt owed by the seller, and explain the rationale and intra-madhhab differences.

Core Idea
In salam, mixing cash and debt capital divides the contract: cash portion valid, debt portion void due to incidental separation.

Salam contracts require immediate payment of the full capital. But what if part of that capital is actually a debt the seller owes the buyer? This lesson unpacks a nuanced Hanafi ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq: the contract stands for the cash but collapses for the debt, with important implications and differences among the early Hanafi masters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case
Recognize the scenario: capital is partly cash (paid now) and partly a debt already owed by the seller. The contract is for a deferred commodity.
The debt portion is not a new payment but an existing obligation.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The salam is valid (sahih) for the cash portion but void (fasid) for the debt portion. If the full capital is paid before separation, the entire contract becomes valid.
The voidness is fasid, not batil – it is a corruption that can be cured.
3
Understand the rationale
The contract was valid at inception because the debt was unspecified. The corruption (separation before receipt) occurs later and is incidental; it only affects the debt portion because that becomes a prohibited debt-for-debt exchange.
Key principle: an incidental corruption does not spread to the valid part.
4
Note the intra-madhhab dispute
Imam Zufar holds the entire salam void. For two-type capital (dirhams and dinars), Abu Hanifa rules impermissible, but the Sahibayn permit it. Know each position.
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) view is Abu Hanifa's for both issues.
5
Apply the principle
In any mixed capital salam, identify which portion is cash and which is debt. Scrutinize whether the capital is of one type or more. Apply the ruling accordingly.
This ruling highlights the strict conditions of salam: capital must be known and paid immediately.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قبل الافتراق، فإن أسلم مائتي درهم في كرّ بر مائةً ديناً عليه، ومائة نقداً، فالسلمُ صفة المائة أي على مسلم إليه أي منقودة في الدين باطل. (عيني، معدن) کر بر: بضم الكاف وتشديد الراء: ستون قفيزا، والقفيز اثنا عشر صاعا (ط) عيني باطل: لافتراقهما عن دين بدين، وليس المعنى أنه انعقد باطلاً في حصة الدين بل هو صحيح، والمفسد طارئ عليه بافتراقهما، فلم يسر الفساد إلى حصة المائة الثانية، ولهذا لو نقد مأتين قبل الافتراق، صح في الكل، وعند زفر: السلم باطل في الكل؛ لأنه جعل القبول في الدين شرطاً لصحته في الآخر، فيفسد في الكل ولنا أن العقد وقع صحيحاً؛ لعدم تعين الدين. ثم فساده في البعض طارئ، فلا يتعدى، وهذا إذا كان رأس المال والمسلم فيه من نوع واحد، أما إذا كان رأس المال من نوعين بأن أسلم إلى رجل في كر بر عشرة من الدراهم المعينة، وعشرة من الدنانير التي عليه، فلا يجوز في حق الدنانير إجماعاً، وفي الدراهم كذلك عنده؛ لجهالة ما يخصها من المسلم فيه، خلافاً لهما، بناء على أن إعلام رأس المال ليس بشرط عندهما، وأما إذا كان المسلم فيه من نوعين بأن أسلم مائة درهم في كر بر وكر شعير، و لم يبين رأس مال كل واحد لا يجوز عنده. (عيني، فتح)
Before separation, if one pays in advance two hundred dirhams for a kurr of wheat, one hundred as a debt upon him and one hundred as cash, then the salam is valid for the one hundred (cash), i.e. the one hundred that are paid, but void regarding the debt. (Ayni, Ma'din) Kurr: with a damma on the kaf and tashdid on the ra', is sixty qafiz, and a qafiz is twelve sa'. (T) Ayni: It is void because they part from one debt for another debt. The meaning is not that the contract was concluded void in the portion of the debt; rather it was valid, and the corrupting factor occurred later due to their separation, so the corruption does not spread to the second hundred. Thus if he paid the two hundred before separation, it would be valid in its entirety. According to Zufar: the salam is void entirely because he made acceptance of the debt a condition for validity in the other, so it corrupts the whole. Our proof: the contract was concluded validly because the debt was not specified. Then its corruption in part was incidental, so it does not extend. This is when the capital and the salam commodity are of one type. But if the capital is of two types, such as one advancing to a man for a kurr of wheat ten specified dirhams and ten dinars which are a debt upon him, then it is not permissible regarding the dinars by consensus, and likewise regarding the dirhams according to him (Abu Hanifa) due to ignorance of what portion of the salam commodity corresponds to them. Contrary to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), based on the view that specifying the capital is not a condition with them. And if the salam commodity is of two types, such as advancing one hundred dirhams for a kurr of wheat and a kurr of barley without specifying the capital for each, it is not permissible according to him (Abu Hanifa). (Ayni, Fath)
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq deals with the ruling of salam when the capital is mixed between cash and a debt owed by the seller. It opens by presenting a case: a man pays 200 dirhams for a kurr of wheat, with 100 being a debt owed by the seller to the buyer, and 100 being actual cash. The ruling is that the salam is valid for the cash portion but void for the debt portion. The commentator, al-Ayni, explains that the reason for the void is that after the contract, the buyer and seller part from the session before payment, and this separation occurs regarding a debt-for-debt exchange, which is prohibited. However, the contract was valid at its inception; the corruption arises afterward due to the separation, so it only affects the debt portion. If the buyer had paid the full 200 before separation, the entire contract would have been valid. Imam Zufar disagrees, holding that the entire salam is void because accepting the debt as part of the capital makes the contract conditional, and failure to deliver the debt portion corrupts the whole. The Hanafi response is that the contract was valid initially because the debt was unspecified; the corruption is incidental and does not extend. The passage then addresses a variant where the capital consists of two types: specified dirhams and dinars owed by the seller. Here, Abu Hanifa rules it impermissible due to ignorance of the portion of the salam commodity for each, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) permit it because they do not require specification of the capital. Finally, if the salam commodity is of two types without specifying capital for each, Abu Hanifa also rules it impermissible. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa, as found in Zahir al-Riwayah. The key legal principle is that salam is a contract of deferred delivery with immediate payment, and any ambiguity or violation of the strict requirements can lead to partial or total invalidity.

Key Terms
سلم (salam): A sale by advance payment where the price is paid immediately and the commodity is delivered later.
رأس المال (ra's al-mal): The principal or capital paid in advance in a salam contract.
مسلم فيه (muslam fihi): The deferred commodity to be delivered in a salam contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man pays 200 dirhams for a kurr of wheat: 100 dirhams as cash and 100 dirhams as a debt owed by the seller. The buyer and seller separate before the buyer receives the wheat. What is the ruling according to the Hanafi school?
A) The entire salam is void.
B) The salam is valid for the cash portion but void for the debt portion.
C) The salam is valid in its entirety because the debt was unspecified.
D) The salam is void only if the debt exceeds the cash portion.

Key Takeaway
When salam capital includes a debt, the cash portion remains valid but the debt portion is void due to separation before receipt; intra-madhhab differences exist but the relied-upon view is Abu Hanifa's.
